They help organize code into logical units, prevent namespace pollution, and enable code reuse across projects. A module is simply a .py file that can contain functions, classes, and variables.</p>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Importing Modules</h2>\n                <p>Python provides several ways to import modules and their contents.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Import Statements:</h4>\n<pre><code># Import entire module\nimport math\nprint(math.sqrt(16))  # 4.0\nprint(math.pi)        # 3.141592653589793\n\n# Import with alias\nimport math as m\nprint(m.sqrt(25))  # 5.0\n\n# Import specific items\nfrom math import sqrt, pi\nprint(sqrt(36))  # 6.0\nprint(pi)        # 3.14159...\n\n# Import multiple items\nfrom math import sin, cos, tan\n\n# Import with alias (specific items)\nfrom math import sqrt as square_root\nprint(square_root(49))  # 7.0\n\n# Import everything (not recommended)\nfrom math import *\n# Now all math functions are available directly\n# But this pollutes the namespace\n\n# Common module aliases (conventions)\nimport numpy as np\nimport pandas as pd\nimport matplotlib.pyplot as plt\nimport seaborn as sns\n\n# Import user-defined module\nimport my_module\nfrom my_module import my_function</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 2-5:</strong> Import the whole module and access items with dot notation.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 8-10:</strong> Use aliases to shorten module names.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 13-16:</strong> Import specific functions or variables from a module.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 24-25:</strong> Avoid <code>from module import *</code> - it pollutes your namespace.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 28-31:</strong> Some modules have conventional aliases everyone uses.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 34-35:</strong> Import your own Python files as modules.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Creating Your Own Modules</h2>\n                <p>Any Python file can be a module. Let\'s create a simple module structure.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Module Example (mymath.py):</h4>\n<pre><code># mymath.py - A custom math utilities module\n\n"""Mathematical utility functions."""\n\nPI = 3.14159\n\ndef circle_area(radius):\n    """Calculate the area of a circle."""\n    return PI * radius ** 2\n\ndef circle_circumference(radius):\n    """Calculate the circumference of a circle."""\n    return 2 * PI * radius\n\ndef rectangle_area(width, height):\n    """Calculate the area of a rectangle."""\n    return width * height\n\n# Code that runs only when executed directly\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    # This block runs when: python mymath.py\n    # It does NOT run when: import mymath\n    print("Testing mymath module:")\n    print(f"Circle area (r=5): {circle_area(5)}")\n    print(f"Circle circumference (r=5): {circle_circumference(5)}")</code></pre>\n                </div>\n\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Using the Module:</h4>\n<pre><code># main.py - Using our custom module\nimport mymath\n\nprint(mymath.PI)                    # 3.14159\nprint(mymath.circle_area(5))        # 78.53975\nprint(mymath.circle_circumference(3))  # 18.84954\n\n# Import specific functions\nfrom mymath import circle_area, PI\n\narea = circle_area(10)\nprint(f"Area: {area}")  # Area: 314.159\n\n# Check what\'s in a module\nimport mymath\nprint(dir(mymath))  # Lists all attributes\n# [\'PI\', \'__builtins__\', \'__cached__\', ... , \'circle_area\', ...]\n\n# Get help on a module\nhelp(mymath)  # Shows docstrings</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 5:</strong> Module-level variables can be constants.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 8-18:</strong> Define functions that will be available when imported.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 21-27:</strong> The <code>if __name__ == "__main__"</code> block runs only when the file is executed directly.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 34-35:</strong> Access module contents with dot notation.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 44-45:</strong> <code>dir()</code> lists all module attributes.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Packages</h2>\n                <p>A package is a collection of modules organized in directories. Packages help structure larger projects and avoid naming conflicts.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Package Structure:</h4>\n<pre><code># Directory structure:\n# mypackage/\n# ├── __init__.py\n# ├── core.py\n# ├── utils.py\n# └── subpackage/\n#     ├── __init__.py\n#     └── helpers.py\n\n# __init__.py can be empty or contain initialization code\n# mypackage/__init__.py\nfrom .core import main_function\nfrom .utils import helper\n\n__version__ = "1.0.0"\n\n# mypackage/core.py\ndef main_function():\n    return "Main function called"\n\ndef internal_function():\n    return "Internal use only"\n\n# mypackage/utils.py\ndef helper():\n    return "Helper function"\n\n# Using the package\nimport mypackage\nprint(mypackage.__version__)  # 1.0.0\nprint(mypackage.main_function())  # Main function called\n\n# Import from submodule\nfrom mypackage import core\nfrom mypackage.utils import helper\n\n# Import from subpackage\nfrom mypackage.subpackage.helpers import something</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 2-8:</strong> Package directory structure with <code>__init__.py</code> files.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 11-15:</strong> <code>__init__.py</code> can define what the package exports.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 24-26:</strong> Import from package uses dot notation.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 29-30:</strong> Import specific modules from the package.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <h4>💡 __init__.py</h4>\n                    <p>The <code>__init__.py</code> file marks a directory as a Python package. It can be empty or contain initialization code. In Python 3.3+, packages can be "namespace packages" without <code>__init__.py</code>, but it\'s still recommended to include it.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Relative vs Absolute Imports</h2>\n                <p>Within packages, you can use relative imports to import from sibling modules.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Import Types:</h4>\n<pre><code># Package structure:\n# myapp/\n# ├── __init__.py\n# ├── models.py\n# ├── views.py\n# └── utils/\n#     ├── __init__.py\n#     ├── helpers.py\n#     └── validators.py\n\n# Absolute imports (recommended)\n# In myapp/views.py:\nfrom myapp.models import User\nfrom myapp.utils.helpers import format_date\nfrom myapp.utils.validators import validate_email\n\n# Relative imports (within package only)\n# In myapp/views.py:\nfrom .models import User          # Same level\nfrom .utils.helpers import format_date  # Subdirectory\n\n# In myapp/utils/helpers.py:\nfrom .validators import validate_email  # Same level\nfrom ..models import User         # Parent level (..)\n\n# In myapp/utils/__init__.py:\nfrom .helpers import format_date\nfrom .validators import validate_email\n\n# Relative import syntax:\n# .     current package\n# ..    parent package\n# ...   grandparent package (rare)\n\n# Avoid circular imports!\n# If A imports B and B imports A, you get a circular import error\n# Solution: Restructure code or import inside functions</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 11-13:</strong> Absolute imports use the full path from the project root.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 16-20:</strong> Relative imports use dots to navigate the package structure.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 23-24:</strong> Use <code>..</code> to import from the parent package.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 32-34:</strong> Circular imports happen when modules import each other.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>The Python Standard Library</h2>\n                <p>Python comes with a rich standard library. Here are some commonly used modules.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Useful Standard Modules:</h4>\n<pre><code># Operating system interface\nimport os\nprint(os.getcwd())           # Current directory\nos.listdir(\'.\')              # List files\nos.environ.get(\'HOME\')       # Environment variables\n\n# Path handling (modern)\nfrom pathlib import Path\nhome = Path.home()\nfile = Path("folder/file.txt")\n\n# System-specific parameters\nimport sys\nprint(sys.version)           # Python version\nprint(sys.argv)              # Command line arguments\n\n# Pattern matching\nimport re\nre.findall(r\'\\d+\', "abc123def456")  # [\'123\', \'456\']\n\n# Mathematics\nimport math\nmath.sqrt(16)    # 4.0\nmath.ceil(4.3)   # 5\n\n# Random numbers\nimport random\nrandom.random()           # 0.0 to 1.0\nrandom.randint(1, 10)     # 1 to 10\nrandom.choice([1, 2, 3])  # Random element\nrandom.shuffle(list_)     #       <p>Virtual environments create isolated Python installations, preventing package conflicts between projects.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Working with Virtual Environments:</h4>\n<pre><code># Create virtual environment\npython -m venv myenv\n\n# Activate (Linux/macOS)\nsource myenv/bin/activate\n\n# Activate (Windows)\nmyenv\\Scripts\\activate\n\n# Deactivate\ndeactivate\n\n# Once activated, pip installs to the virtual environment\npip install requests  # Only in this environment\n\n# Create with specific Python version\npython3.11 -m venv myenv\n\n# Virtual environment structure:\n# myenv/\n# ├── bin/ (Linux/macOS) or Scripts/ (Windows)\n# │   ├── activate\n# │   ├── python\n# │   └── pip\n# ├── dependency management)\npip install poetry\npoetry new myproject\npoetry add requests  # Add dependency\n\n# Using conda (Anaconda/Miniconda)\nconda create -n myenv python=3.11\nconda activate                  </div>\n                </div>\n\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <h4>💡 Always Use Virtual Environments</h4>\n                    <p>Never install project dependencies globally. Web APIs (specifically REST APIs) use HTTP to exchange data. Python makes it easy to consume APIs, allowing you to fetch data from services like weather APIs, social media, financial data, and more.</p>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>HTTP Basics</h2>\n                <p>HTTP (Hypertext Transfer Protocol) is the foundation of web APIs. Understanding HTTP methods and status codes is essential for working with APIs.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>HTTP Methods:</h4>\n<pre><code># HTTP Methods (verbs):\n# GET     - Retrieve data\n# POST    - Create new data\n# PUT     - Update existing data (full replace)\n# PATCH   - Partially update data\n# DELETE  - Remove data\n\n# Common HTTP Status Codes:\n# 200 OK              - Request succeeded\n# 201 Created         - Resource created successfully\n# 204 No Content      - Success, no body returned\n# 400 Bad Request     - Invalid request format\n# 401 Unauthorized    - Authentication required\n# 403 Forbidden       - Access denied\n# 404 Not Found       - Resource doesn\'t exist\n# 429 Too Many Requests - Rate limit exceeded\n# 500 Internal Error  - Server error\n\n# Request Components:\n# - URL (endpoint)\n# - Method (GET, POST, etc.)\n# - Headers (metadata, authentication)\n# - Body (data for POST/PUT)\n# - Query parameters (for GET)\n\n# Example URL with query parameters:\n# https://api.example.com/users?page=2&limit=10&sort=name</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 3-8:</strong> HTTP methods correspond to CRUD operations (Create, Read, Update, Delete).</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 11-20:</strong> Status codes indicate the result of the request.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 23-27:</strong> Requests have several components that control behavior.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Line 30:</strong> Query parameters filter and customize GET requests.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Using the requests Library</h2>\n                <p>The requests library is Python\'s most popular HTTP client. It\'s simple, elegant, and handles most HTTP operations easily.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Making GET Requests:</h4>\n<pre><code>import requests\n\n# Simple GET request\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.github.com")\nprint(response.status_code)  # 200\nprint(response.ok)           # True (status < 400)\n\n# Get response as text\nprint(response.text)\n\n# Get response as JSON (most common for APIs)\ndata = response.json()\nprint(data["current_user_url"])\n\n# Check content type\nprint(response.headers["Content-Type"])\n\n# GET with query parameters\nparams = {"q": "python", "sort": "stars", "order": "desc"}\nresponse = requests.get(\n    "https://api.github.com/search/repositories",\n    params=params\n)\ndata = response.json()\nprint(f"Found {data[\'total_count\']} repositories")\n\n# GET with headers\nheaders = {\n    "User-Agent": "MyApp/1.0",\n    "Accept": "application/json"\n}\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.github.com", headers=headers)\n\n# Handling errors\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.github.com/nonexistent")\nif response.status_code == 404:\n    print("Resource not found")\n\n# Raise exception for HTTP errors\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.github.com/nonexistent")\nresponse.raise_for_status()  # Raises HTTPError for 4xx/5xx\n\n# Safe request with error handling\ntry:\n    response = requests.get("https://api.example.com/data")\n    response.raise_for_status()\n    data = response.json()\nexcept requests.exceptions.HTTPError as e:\n    print(f"HTTP error: {e}")\nexcept requests.exceptions.ConnectionError:\n    print("Connection failed")\nexcept requests.exceptions.JSONDecodeError:\n    print("Invalid JSON response")</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 4-6:</strong> Make a simple GET request and check the response.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 9-12:</strong> Access response content as text or parsed JSON.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 16-23:</strong> Pass query parameters as a dictionary.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 26-30:</strong> Add headers for metadata and authentication.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 38-39:</strong> <code>raise_for_status()</code> raises an exception for HTTP errors.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 42-51:</strong> Handle various types of request errors.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>POST, PUT, and DELETE Requests</h2>\n                <p>Most APIs require sending data to create, update, or delete resources. The requests library handles these operations seamlessly.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Sending Data:</h4>\n<pre><code>import requests\n\n# POST request (create resource)\nnew_user = {\n    "name": "John Doe",\n    "email": "john@example.com"\n}\nresponse = requests.post(\n    "https://api.example.com/users",\n    json=new_user  # Automatically sets Content-Type header\n)\ncreated_user = response.json()\nprint(f"Created user with ID: {created_user[\'id\']}")\n\n# POST with form data\nform_data = {"username": "john", "password": "secret"}\nresponse = requests.post(\n    "https://api.example.com/login",\n    data=form_data  # Sends as application/x-www-form-urlencoded\n)\n\n# POST with files\nfiles = {"file": open("document.pdf", "rb")}\nresponse = requests.post(\n    "https://api.example.com/upload",\n    files=files\n)\n\n# PUT request (update/replace)\nupdated_user = {\n    "name": "John Smith",\n    "email": "johnsmith@example.com"\n}\nresponse = requests.put(\n    "https://api.example.com/users/123",\n    json=updated_user\n)\n\n# PATCH request (partial update)\npatch_data = {"email": "newemail@example.com"}\nresponse = requests.patch(\n    "https://api.example.com/users/123",\n    json=patch_data\n)\n\n# DELETE request\nresponse = requests.delete("https://api.example.com/users/123")\nif response.status_code == 204:\n    print("User deleted successfully")\n\n# PUT vs PATCH:\n# PUT replaces the entire resource\n# PATCH updates only specified fields</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 4-14:</strong> POST creates resources. Use <code>json=</code> to send JSON data.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 17-21:</strong> Use <code>data=</code> for form-encoded data.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 24-28:</strong> Upload files using the <code>files=</code> parameter.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 31-38:</strong> PUT replaces an entire resource.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 41-45:</strong> PATCH updates only specific fields.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 48-50:</strong> DELETE removes a resource, often returns 204.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Authentication</h2>\n                <p>Many APIs require authentication. The requests library supports various authentication methods.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Authentication Methods:</h4>\n<pre><code>import requests\nfrom requests.auth import HTTPBasicAuth\n\n# API Key in header\nheaders = {"X-API-Key": "your-api-key-here"}\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.example.com/data", headers=headers)\n\n# API Key in query parameter\nparams = {"api_key": "your-api-key-here"}\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.example.com/data", params=params)\n\n# Bearer token (OAuth 2.0)\nheaders = {"Authorization": "Bearer your-token-here"}\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.example.com/protected", headers=headers)\n\n# Basic authentication\nresponse = requests.get(\n    "https://api.example.com/protected",\n    auth=HTTPBasicAuth("username", "password")\n)\n# Or simply:\nresponse = requests.get(\n    "https://api.example.com/protected",\n    auth=("username", "password")\n)\n\n# Session with persistent authentication\nsession = requests.Session()\nsession.headers.update({"Authorization": "Bearer your-token"})\n\n# All requests with this session include the header\nresponse1 = session.get("https://api.example.com/data1")\nresponse2 = session.get("https://api.example.com/data2")\n\n# Session with automatic retry\nfrom requests.adapters import HTTPAdapter\nfrom urllib3.util.retry import Retry\n\nsession = requests.Session()\nretry = Retry(\n    total=3,\n    backoff_factor=1,\n    status_forcelist=[500, 502, 503, 504]\n)\nadapter = HTTPAdapter(max_retries=retry)\nsession.mount("https://", adapter)\nsession.mount("http://", adapter)</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 5-6:</strong> API key in a custom header (common pattern).</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 9-10:</strong> Some APIs accept the key as a query parameter.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 13-14:</strong> Bearer tokens are standard for OAuth 2.0.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 17-24:</strong> Basic auth sends username/password encoded in header.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 27-33:</strong> Sessions persist headers across multiple requests.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 36-46:</strong> Configure automatic retries for failed requests.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Working with JSON</h2>\n                <p>JSON is the most common data format for APIs. Python and JSON work together seamlessly.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>JSON Operations:</h4>\n<pre><code>import json\nimport requests\n\n# Python dict to JSON string\ndata = {"name": "Alice", "age": 25, "active": True}\njson_string = json.dumps(data)\nprint(json_string)  # {"name": "Alice", "age": 25, "active": true}\n\n# JSON string to Python dict\nparsed = json.loads(json_string)\nprint(parsed["name"])  # Alice\n\n# Pretty print JSON\nprint(json.dumps(data, indent=2))\n# {\n#   "name": "Alice",\n#   "age": 25,\n#   "active": true\n# }\n\n# Save JSON to file\nwith open("data.json", "w") as f:\n    json.dump(data, f, indent=2)\n\n# Load JSON from file\nwith open("data.json", "r") as f:\n    loaded = json.load(f)\n\n# Working with API response\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.github.com/users/python")\nuser = response.json()\n\nprint(f"User: {user[\'login\']}")\nprint(f"Name: {user[\'name\']}")\nprint(f"Followers: {user[\'followers\']}")\n\n# Handle nested JSON\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.github.com/repos/python/cpython")\nrepo = response.json()\n\nprint(f"Repo: {repo[\'full_name\']}")\nprint(f"Stars: {repo[\'stargazers_count\']}")\nprint(f"Language: {repo[\'language\']}")\n\n# Complex nested data\nfor commit in repo_data["commits"]:\n    print(f"Author: {commit[\'author\'][\'name\']}")\n    print(f"Message: {commit[\'message\'][:50]}")</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 5-6:</strong> <code>json.dumps()</code> converts Python objects to JSON string.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 9-10:</strong> <code>json.loads()</code> parses JSON string to Python objects.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 13-20:</strong> Use <code>indent</code> for readable JSON output.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 23-27:</strong> <code>json.dump/load</code> work directly with files.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 30-35:</strong> Response objects have a <code>.json()</code> method.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 45-47:</strong> Access nested data with chained brackets.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Building an API Client Class</h2>\n                <p>Creating a dedicated client class makes working with an API cleaner and more maintainable.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>API Client Pattern:</h4>\n<pre><code>import requests\nfrom typing import Optional, Dict, Any\n\nclass APIClient:\n    """A reusable API client with error handling."""\n    \n    def __init__(self, base_url: str, api_key: str):\n        self.base_url = base_url.rstrip("/")\n        self.session = requests.Session()\n        self.session.headers.update({\n            "Authorization": f"Bearer {api_key}",\n            "Accept": "application/json"\n        })\n    \n    def _request(\n        self,\n        method: str,\n        endpoint: str,\n        **kwargs\n    ) -> Optional[Dict[str, Any]]:\n        """Make an HTTP request with error handling."""\n        url = f"{self.base_url}/{endpoint.lstrip(\'/\')}"\n        \n        try:\n            response = self.session.request(method, url, **kwargs)\n            response.raise_for_status()\n            return response.json() if response.content else None\n        except requests.exceptions.HTTPError as e:\n            print(f"HTTP Error: {e}")\n            return None\n        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:\n            print(f"Request Error: {e}")\n            return None\n    \n    def get(self, endpoint: str, params: dict = None):\n        """GET request."""\n        return self._request("GET", endpoint, params=params)\n    \n    def post(self, endpoint: str, data: dict = None):\n        """POST request."""\n        return self._request("POST", endpoint, json=data)\n    \n    def put(self, endpoint: str, data: dict = None):\n        """PUT request."""\n        return self._request("PUT", endpoint, json=data)\n    \n    def delete(self, endpoint: str):\n        """DELETE request."""\n        return self._request("DELETE", endpoint)\n\n# Using the client\nclient = APIClient("https://api.example.com", "your-api-key")\n\n# Get all users\nusers = client.get("/users")\n\n# Create a user\nnew_user = client.post("/users", data={"name": "Alice"})\n\n# Update a user\nclient.put("/users/1", data={"name": "Alice Smith"})\n\n# Delete a user\nclient.delete("/users/1")</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 8-14:</strong> Initialize with base URL and set up session with auth headers.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 16-32:</strong> Private method handles all requests with error handling.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 34-46:</strong> Public methods for each HTTP verb.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 49-62:</strong> Using the client is clean and intuitive.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Practical Example: Weather API</h2>\n                <p>Let\'s build a practical weather application using a real API.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Weather Client:</h4>\n<pre><code>import requests\n\nclass WeatherClient:\n    """Client for OpenWeatherMap API."""\n    \n    BASE_URL = "https://api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5"\n    \n    def __init__(self, api_key: str):\n        self.api_key = api_key\n    \n    def get_weather(self, city: str) -> dict:\n        """Get current weather for a city."""\n        params = {\n            "q": city,\n            "appid": self.api_key,\n            "units": "metric"\n        }\n        \n        response = requests.get(\n            f"{self.BASE_URL}/weather",\n            params=params\n        )\n        response.raise_for_status()\n        return response.json()\n    \n    def get_forecast(self, city: str, days: int = 5) -> dict:\n        """Get weather forecast for a city."""\n        params = {\n            "q": city,\n            "appid": self.api_key,\n            "units": "metric",\n            "cnt": days * 8  # 8 forecasts per day\n        }\n        \n        response = requests.get(\n            f"{self.BASE_URL}/forecast",\n            params=params\n        )\n        response.raise_for_status()\n        return response.json()\n\ndef display_weather(weather_data: dict):\n    """Display weather information."""\n    city = weather_data["name"]\n    temp = weather_data["main"]["temp"]\n    description = weather_data["weather"][0]["description"]\n    humidity = weather_data["main"]["humidity"]\n    wind = weather_data["wind"]["speed"]\n    \n    print(f"\\nWeather in {city}:")\n    print(f" <p><strong>Lines 6-8:</strong> Store constants at class level.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 12-25:</strong> Method to fetch current weather with proper error handling.</p>\n class="content-section">\n                <h2>Rate Limiting and Caching</h2>\n                <p>Real-world API usage requires handling rate limits and caching responses to avoid unnecessary requests.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Rate Limiting:</h4>\n<pre><code>import time\nimport requests\nfrom functools import wraps\n\n# Simple rate limiter\ndef rate_limit(calls_per_second: float = 2):\n    """Decorator to limit API call rate."""\n    min_interval = 1.0 / calls_per_second\n    last_call = [0.0]\n    \n    def decorator(func):\n        @wraps(func)\n        def wrapper(*args, **kwargs):\n            elapsed = time.time() - last_call[0]\n            if elapsed < min_interval:\n                time.sleep(min_interval - elapsed)\n            last_call[0] = time.time()\n            return func(*args, **kwargs)\n        return wrapper\n    return decorator\n\n@rate_limit(calls_per_second=2)\ndef api_call(url):\n    return requests.get(url)\n\n# Simple cache\nimport json\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nclass CachedAPI:\n    def __init__(self, cache_dir: str = "cache"):\n        self.cache_dir = Path(cache_dir)\n        self.cache_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)\n    \n    def get(self, url: str, expire_seconds: int = 3600):\n        """Get data with caching."""\n        cache_file = self.cache_dir / f"{hash(url)}.json"\n        \n        # Check cache\n        if cache_file.exists():\n            age = time.time() - cache_file.stat().st_mtime\n            if age < expire_seconds:\n                with open(cache_file) as f:\n                    return json.load(f)\n        \n        # Fetch fresh data\n        response = requests.get(url)\n        data = response.json()\n        \n        # Save to cache\n        with open(cache_file, "w") as f:\n            json.dump(data, f)\n        \n        return data\n\n# Using requests-cache (third-party library)\n# pip install requests-cache\nimport requests_cache\n\n# Cache all requests automatically\nrequests_cache.install_cache(\n    cache_name="api_cache",\n    backend="sqlite",\n    expire_after=3600  # 1 hour\n)\n\n# Now regular requests.get() is cached\nresponse = requests.get("https://api.example.com/data")\nprint(response.from_cache)  # True if from cache</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 6-20:</strong> Decorator to limit request rate.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 25-49:</strong> Manual caching implementation with expiration.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 53-66:</strong> <code>requests-cache</code> library provides automatic caching.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n Good practices make your code easier to read, debug, and scale. They help teams collaborate effectively and reduce technical debt. Following the Python community\'s conventions ensures your code is accessible to other developers.</p>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>PEP 8: Python Style Guide</h2>\n                <p>PEP 8 is the official Python style guide. Following it makes your code consistent with the broader Python community.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Key Style Guidelines:</h4>\n<pre><code># Naming Conventions\nmy_variable = "snake_case"        # Variables and functions\nMyClass = "PascalCase"            # Classes\nMY_CONSTANT = "UPPER_SNAKE_CASE"  # Constants\n_private_var = "leading_underscore"  # Internal use\n\ndef my_function(param_one, param_two):\n    """Function with descriptive name and docstring."""\n    pass\n\n# Indentation: 4 spaces (not tabs)\ndef example():\n    if True:\n        do_something()  # 4 spaces\n\n# Line length: 79 characters max\n# Long lines can be broken with parentheses\nresult = some_function(\n    arg_one,\n    arg_two,\n    arg_three\n)\n\n# Blank lines\n# 2 blank lines before top-level functions/classes\n# 1 blank line between methods\n\ndef function_one():\n    pass\n\n\ndef function_two():\n    pass\n\n\nclass MyClass:\n    def method_one(self):\n        pass\n    \n    def method_two(self):\n        pass\n\n# Imports: one per line, grouped\nimport os\nimport sys\nfrom collections import defaultdict, Counter\nfrom mypackage import mymodule\n\n# Whitespace\nspam(ham[1], {eggs: 2})  # No space inside brackets\nif x == 4:               # Space around operators\n    print(x, y)          # No space before colon in slices\nmy_list[1:9:3]           # No spaces in slice expressions\n\n# Comparison operators\nif x is None:            # Compare to None with \'is\'\nif x is not None:\nif my_list:              # Check empty collections truthiness\nif not my_list:</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 2-6:</strong> Use snake_case for variables/functions, PascalCase for classes.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 14-19:</strong> Use 4 spaces for indentation and break long lines with parentheses.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 22-38:</strong> Use appropriate blank lines to separate code sections.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 41-44:</strong> Group imports: standard library, third-party, local.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 47-50:</strong> Avoid extraneous whitespace inside brackets.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 56-58:</strong> Use <code>is</code> for None comparisons, not <code>==</code>.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <h4>💡 Automatic Formatting</h4>\n                    <p>Use tools like <code>black</code> (formatter), <code>flake8</code> (linter), and <code>isort</code> (import sorter) to automatically format and check your code.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Writing Clean Functions</h2>\n                <p>Functions should do one thing, do it well, and have clear names. This makes code testable and reusable.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Function Best Practices:</h4>\n<pre><code># Good: Single responsibility\ndef calculate_discount(price, discount_rate):\n    """Calculate the discounted price."""\n    return price * (1 - discount_rate)\n\ndef format_price(price):\n    """Format price as currency string."""\n    return f"${price:.2f}"\n\n# Bad: Multiple responsibilities\ndef calculate_and_print_discount(price, discount_rate):\n    total = price * (1 - discount_rate)\n    print(f"Discounted price: ${total:.2f}")\n    # Mixing calculation and output is bad\n\n# Good: Type hints for clarity\ndef get_user_age(user_id: int) -> int:\n    """Get user age by ID.\n    \n    Args:\n        user_id: The user\'s unique identifier\n        \n    Returns:\n        The user\'s age in years\n        \n    Raises:\n        UserNotFoundError: If user doesn\'t exist\n    """\n    user = database.get_user(user_id)\n    return user.age\n\n# Good: Default arguments for flexibility\ndef create_user(\n    name: str,\n    email: str,\n    role: str = "user",\n    active: bool = True\n) -> dict:\n    return {\n        "name": name,\n        "email": email,\n        "role": role,\n        "active": active\n    }\n\n# Avoid mutable default arguments!\n# Bad - the list is shared across all calls\ndef add_item(item, items=[]):\n    items.append(item)\n    return items\n\n# Good - use None and create inside function\ndef add_item(item, items=None):\n    if items is None:\n        items = []\n    items.append(item)\n    return items\n\n# Keep functions small (under 20-30 lines)\n# Extract complex logic into helper functions</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 2-9:</strong> Each function should do one thing.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 12-16:</strong> Avoid mixing calculations with I/O operations.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 19-32:</strong> Use type hints and thorough docstrings.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 35-47:</strong> Default arguments make functions more flexible.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 50-59:</strong> Never use mutable default arguments - use None instead.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Error Handling Patterns</h2>\n                <p>Good error handling makes your code robust and helps with debugging. Follow these patterns for professional code.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Error Handling Best Practices:</h4>\n<pre><code># Be specific about exceptions\n# Bad\ntry:\n    do_something()\nexcept Exception:  # Too broad\n    pass\n\n# Good\ntry:\n    do_something()\nexcept (ValueError, KeyError) as e:\n    logger.error(f"Operation failed: {e}")\n    raise\n\n# Use custom exceptions for domain errors\nclass PaymentError(Exception):\n    """Base exception for payment errors."""\n    pass\n\nclass InsufficientFundsError(PaymentError):\n    """Account has insufficient funds."""\n    def __init__(self, balance, amount):\n        self.balance = balance\n        self.amount = amount\n        super().__init__(\n            f"Insufficient funds: {balance} available, "\n            f"{amount} required"\n        )\n\n# Handle at the right level\ndef process_payment(user_id, amount):\n    # Low-level: let exceptions propagate\n    user = get_user(user_id)\n    if user.balance < amount:\n        raise InsufficientFundsError(user.balance, amount)\n    return charge_user(user, amount)\n\ndef checkout(user_id, cart_total):\n    # High-level: handle and present to user\n    try:\n        receipt = process_payment(user_id, cart_total)\n        return {"success": True, "receipt": receipt}\n    except InsufficientFundsError as e:\n        return {\n            "success": False,\n            "error": "insufficient_funds",\n            "message": str(e)\n        }\n    except PaymentError as e:\n        logger.error(f"Payment failed: {e}")\n        return {"success": False, "error": "payment_failed"}\n\n# Use context managers for cleanup\nfrom contextlib import contextmanager\n\n@contextmanager\ndef database_transaction():\n    conn = get_connection()\n    try:\n        yield conn\n        conn.commit()\n    except Exception:\n        conn.rollback()\n        raise\n    finally:\n        conn.close()\n\n# Usage\nwith database_transaction() as conn:\n    conn.execute("INSERT INTO users VALUES (?)", (user,))</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 3-11:</strong> Catch specific exceptions, not broad Exception.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 14-27:</strong> Create custom exceptions with meaningful information.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 30-47:</strong> Let exceptions propagate from low-level, handle at high-level.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 50-66:</strong> Use context managers for automatic cleanup.</p>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Testing Your Code</h2>\n                <p>Writing tests ensures your code works correctly and helps prevent regressions. Use pytest for clean, readable tests.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Testing with pytest:</h4>\n<pre><code># test_calculator.py\nimport pytest\nfrom calculator import add, divide, Calculator\n\n# Simple test\ndef test_add():\n    assert add(2, 3) == 5\n    assert add(-1, 1) == 0\n    assert add(0, 0) == 0\n\n# Test with exception\ndef test_divide_by_zero():\n    with pytest.raises(ValueError):\n        divide(10, 0)\n\n# Parameterized tests\n@pytest.mark.parametrize("a,b,expected", [\n    (2, 3, 5),\n    (0, 0, 0),\n    (-1, 1, def test_subtract(self, calculator):\n        assert calculator.subtract(5, 3) == 2\n    \n    def test_multiply(self, calculator):\n        assert calculator.multiply(3, 4) == 12\n\n# Mock external \n        result = fetch_data("http://example.com")\n        \n        assert result == {"key": "value"}\n        mock_get.assert_called_once_with("http://example.com")\n\n# Run tests: pytest        <p><strong>Lines 13-15:</strong> Use <code>pytest.raises</code> to test exceptions.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 18-26:</strong> Parameterized tests run the same test with <h2>Documentation</h2>\n                <p>Good documentation helps others (and future you) understand your code. Python has built-in support for documentation.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Documenting Code:</h4>\n<pre><code>"""\nModule-level docstring.\nDescribe what this module does.\n"""\n\nclass UserService:\n    """Service for managing user operations.\n    \n    This class provides methods for creating, updating,\n    and deleting users in the system.\n    \n    Attributes:\n        db: Database connection instance\n        cache: Optional cache for user data\n    \n    Example:\n        >>> service = UserService(database)\n        >>> user = service.get_user(1)\n        >>> print(user.name)\n        \'Alice\'\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(self, db, cache=None):\n        """Initialize the user service.\n        \n        Args:\n            db: Database connection\n            cache: Optional cache backend (default: None)\n        """\n        self.db = db\n        self.cache = cache\n    \n    def get_user(self, user_id: int) -> dict:\n        """Retrieve a user by ID.\n        \n        Args:\n            user_id: The unique identifier for the user\n        \n        Returns:\n            Dictionary containing user data\n        \n        Raises:\n            UserNotFoundError: If user with given ID doesn\'t exist\n            DatabaseError: If database operation fails\n        \n        Example:\n            >>> user = service.get_user(1)\n            >>> user[\'name\']\n            \'Alice\'\n        """\n        if self.cache:\n            cached = self.cache.get(f"user:{user_id}")\n            if cached:\n                return cached\n        \n        user = self.db.query(\n            "SELECT * FROM users WHERE id = ?",\n            (user_id,)\n        )\n        \n        if not user:\n            raise UserNotFoundError(user_id)\n        \n        return user\n\n\n# README.md for projects\n"""\n# My Project\n\n## Installation\npip install myproject\n\n## Usage\nfrom myproject import Client\nclient = Client()\nresult = client.do_something()\n\n## Contributing\nPull requests welcome!\n\n## License\nMIT\n"""</code></pre>\n                    <div class="code-explanation">\n                        <p><strong>Lines 2-5:</strong> Module docstrings describe the entire module.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 8-26:</strong> Class docstrings include attributes and usage examples.</p>\n                        <p><strong>Lines 34-36:</strong> <code>__init__</code> docstrings               <h2>Final Project: Task Manager CLI</h2>\n                <p>Let\'s build a complete task manager application that demonstrates all the concepts we\'ve learned.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Project Structure:</h4>\n<pre><code># task_manager/\n# ├── __init__.py\n# ├── models.py\n# ├── storage.py\n# ├── manager.py\n# └── cli.py\n\n# models.py\n"""Data models for the task manager."""\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass, field\nfrom datetime import datetime\nfrom typing import Optional\nfrom enum import Enum\n\nclass Priority(Enum):\n    LOW = "low"\n    MEDIUM = "medium"\n    HIGH = "high"\n\nclass Status(Enum):\n    PENDING = "pending"\n    IN_PROGRESS = "in_progress"\n    COMPLETED = "completed"\n\n@dataclass\nclass Task:\n    """Represents a task in the system."""\n    title: str\n    description: str = ""\n    priority: Priority = Priority.MEDIUM\n    status: Status = Status.PENDING\n    id: Optional[int] = None\n    created_at: datetime = field(default_factory=datetime.now)\n    completed_at: Optional[datetime] = None\n    \n    def mark_complete(self):\n        """Mark the task as completed."""\n        self.status = Status.COMPLETED\n        self.completed_at = datetime.now()\n    \n    def __str__(self):\n        status_icon = "✓" if self.status == Status.COMPLETED else "○"\n        return f"[{status_icon}] {self.id}. {self.title} ({self.priority.value})"</code></pre>\n                </div>\n\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>Storage and Manager:</h4>\n<pre><code># storage.py\n"""Persistent storage for tasks."""\nimport json\nfrom pathlib import Path\nfrom typing import List, Optional\nfrom .models import Task, Priority, Status\n\nclass TaskStorage:\n    """Handle persistent storage of tasks."""\n    \n    def __init__(self, filepath: str = "tasks.json"):\n        self.filepath = Path(filepath)\n    \n    def load_all(self) -> List[Task]:\n        """Load all tasks from storage."""\n        if not self.filepath.exists():\n            return []\n        \n        with open(self.filepath) as f:\n            data = json.load(f)\n        \n        return [self._deserialize(item) for item in data]\n    \n    def save_all(self, tasks: List[Task]):\n        """Save all tasks to storage."""\n        data = [self._serialize(task) for task in tasks]\n        with open(self.filepath, "w") as f:\n            json.dump(data, f, indent=2, default=str)\n    \n    def _serialize(self, task: Task) -> dict:\n        """Convert Task to dictionary."""\n        return {\n            "id": task.id,\n            "title": task.title,\n            "description": task.description,\n            "priority": task.priority.value,\n            "status": task.status.value,\n            "created_at": task.created_at.isoformat(),\n            "completed_at": task.completed_at.isoformat() if task.completed_at else None\n        }\n    \n    def _deserialize(self, data: dict) -> Task:\n        """Convert dictionary to Task."""\n        return Task(\n            id=data["id"],\n            title=data["title"],\n            description=data["description"],\n            priority=Priority(data["priority"]),\n            status=Status(data["status"]),\n            created_at=datetime.fromisoformat(data["created_at"]),\n            completed_at=datetime.fromisoformat(data["completed_at"]) if data["completed_at"] else None\n        )\n\n# manager.py\n"""Task management logic."""\nfrom typing import List, Optional\nfrom .models import Task, Priority, Status\nfrom .storage import TaskStorage\n\nclass TaskManager:\n    """Manage task operations."""\n    \n    def __init__(self, storage: TaskStorage):\n        self.storage = storage\n        self._tasks: List[Task] = []\n        self._load_tasks()\n    \n    def _load_tasks(self):\n        """Load tasks from storage."""\n        self._tasks = self.storage.load_all()\n    \n    def _save_tasks(self):\n        """Save tasks to storage."""\n        self.storage.save_all(self._tasks)\n    \n    def _next_id(self) -> int:\n        """Get the next available ID."""\n        if not self._tasks:\n            return 1\n        return max(t.id for t in self._tasks if t.id) + 1\n    \n    def add_task(\n        self,\n        title: str,\n        description: str = "",\n        priority: Priority = Priority.MEDIUM\n    ) -> Task:\n        """Add a new task."""\n        task = Task(\n            id=self._next_id(),\n            title=title,\n            description=description,\n            priority=priority\n        )\n        self._tasks.append(task)\n        self._save_tasks()\n        return task\n    \n    def get_task(self, task_id: int) -> Optional[Task]:\n        """Get a task by ID."""\n        for task in self._tasks:\n            if task.id == task_id:\n                return task\n        return None\n    \n    def complete_task(self, task_id: int) -> Optional[Task]:\n        """Mark a task as completed."""\n        task = self.get_task(task_id)\n        if task:\n            task.mark_complete()\n            self._save_tasks()\n        return task\n    \n    def delete_task(self, task_id: int) -> bool:\n        """Delete a task by ID."""\n        task = self.get_task(task_id)\n        if task:\n            self._tasks.remove(task)\n            self._save_tasks()\n            return True\n        return False\n    \n    def list_tasks(\n        self,\n        status: Optional[Status] = None,\n        priority: Optional[Priority] = None\n    ) -> List[Task]:\n        """List tasks with optional filters."""\n        tasks = self._tasks\n        if status:\n            tasks = [t for t in tasks if t.status == status]\n        if priority:\n            tasks = [t for t in tasks if t.priority == priority]\n        return sorted(tasks, key=lambda t: t.id)</code></pre>\n                </div>\n\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <h4>CLI Interface:</h4>\n<pre><code># cli.py\n"""Command-line interface for       parser = self._create_parser()\n        parsed = parser.parse_args(args)\n        \n        if parsed.command is None:\n            parser.print_help()\n            return\n        \n        command = getattr(self, f"cmd_{parsed.command}")\n        command(parsed)\n    \n    def _create_parser(self):\n        """Create argument parser."""\n        parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(\n            description="Task Manager CLI"\n        )\n        subparsers = parser.add_subparsers(dest="command")\n        \n        # Add command\n        add_parser = subparsers.add_parser("add", help="Add a task")\n        add_parser.add_argument("title", help="Task title")\n        add_parser.add_argument("-d", "--description", default="")\n        add_parser.add_argument("-p", "--priority", \n            choices=["low", "medium", "high"], default="medium")\n        \n        # List command\n        list_parser = subparsers.add_parser("list", help="List tasks")\n "high"])\n        \n        # Complete command\n        complete_parser = subparsers.add_parser("complete", help="Complete task")\n        complete_parser.add_argument("id", type=int, help="Task     return parser\n    \n    def cmd_add(self, args):\n        """Add a new task."""\n        priority = Priority(args.priority)\n        task = self.manager.add_task(\n            title=args.title,\n            description=args.description,\n            priority=priority\n        )\n        print(f"Added task {task.id}: {task.title}")\n    \n    def cmd_list(self, args):\n        """List tasks."""\n        status = Status(args.status) if args.status else None\n        priority = Priority(args.priority) if args.priority else None\n        \n        tasks = self.manager.list_tasks(status, priority)\n        \n        if not tasks:\n            print("No tasks found.")\n            return\n        \n        for task in tasks:\n            print(task)\n    \n    def cmd_complete(self, args):\n        """Complete a task."""\n        task = self.manager.complete_task(args.id)\n        if task:\n            print(f"Completed task {task.id}: {task.title}")\n        else:\n            print(f"Task {args.id} not found.")\n    \n    def cmd_delete(self, args):\n        """Delete a task."""\n        if self.manager.delete_task(args.id):\n            print(f"Deleted task {args.id}")\n        else:\n            print(f"Task {args.id} not found.")\n\ndef main():\n    """Entry point for the CLI."""\n    cli = TaskCLI()\n    cli.run()\n\nif
